Forrester">\n          Forrester\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/John_D._Olivas" title="John D. Olivas">\n          Olivas\n         </a>\n         .\n         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n           Space Shuttle program\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div style="width:100%">\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">\n           \xe2\x86\x90\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n            STS-116\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n            STS-118\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x86\x92\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        STS-117\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS_assembly_sequence" title="ISS assembly sequence">\n        ISS assembly\n       </a>\n       flight\n       <b>\n        13A\n       </b>\n       ) was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       mission flown by\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Atlantis\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , launched from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        pad 39A\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       on 8 June 2007.\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       lifted off from the launch pad at 19:38 EDT. Damage from a hail storm on 26 February 2007 had previously caused the launch to be postponed from an originally-planned launch date of 15 March 2007. The launch of STS-117 marked the 250th orbital\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_human_spaceflights" title="List of human spaceflights">\n        human spaceflight\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       delivered to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS) the second\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starboard" title="Starboard">\n        starboard\n       </a>\n       truss segment (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        S3/S4 Truss\n       </a>\n       ) and its associated energy systems, including a set of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS_Solar_Arrays" title="ISS Solar Arrays">\n        solar arrays\n       </a>\n       . During the course of the mission the crew installed the new truss segment, retracted one set of solar arrays, and unfolded the new set on the starboard side of the station. STS-117 also brought\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_15" title="Expedition 15">\n        Expedition 15\n       </a>\n       crewmember\n       <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Anderson" title="Clayton Anderson">\n        Clayton Anderson\n       </a>\n       to the station, and returned with ISS crewmember\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunita_Williams" title="Sunita Williams">\n        Sunita Williams\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 11 June 2007, NASA mission managers announced a two-day extension of the mission, adding a fourth\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n        extra-vehicular activity\n       </a>\n       (EVA). These two days were inserted into the mission timeline after flight day 8. This possibility had been discussed prior to launch. Because of launch day and thus rendezvous day uncertainty the decision to extend was deferred until after launch. The repair of the gap in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Maneuvering_System" title="Orbital Maneuvering System">\n        Orbital Maneuvering System\n       </a>\n       (OMS) thermal blanket (heat shielding) was conducted during EVA 3.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR14_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR14-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       STS-117 remains the longest mission for\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       because of the cancellation of landing opportunities on 21 June 2007 due to bad weather.\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       landed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n        Edwards Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       on 22 June 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n Forrester\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 3\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">\n          Richard Mastracchio\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         Second spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Mission Specialist 4\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <a href="/wiki/Joan_Higginbotham" title="Joan Higginbotham">\n          Joan Higginbotham\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         First spaceflight\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Astronaut\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_Polansky" title="Mark Polansky">\n        Mark Polansky\n       </a>\n       was originally slated to pilot this mission, but was moved to\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n        STS-116\n       </a>\n       , which he commanded. Also assigned to the flight were\n       <a href="/wiki/Joan_Higginbotham" title="Joan Higginbotham">\n        Joan Higginbotham\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">\n        Richard Mastracchio\n       </a>\n       , who were moved to missions STS-116 and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       respectively.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_payload">\n        Mission payload\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span OBSS 201\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         450 kilograms (990\xc2\xa0lb)?\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Port Sill\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         RMS 301\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         390 kilograms (860\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Total:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          19,083 kilograms (42,071\xc2\xa0lb)\n         </b>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="S3/S4_truss_segments">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="S3.2FS4_truss_segments">\n        S3/S4 truss segments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: S3/S4 truss segments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        Integrated_Truss_Structure\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         For comprehensive description of the S3/S4 truss segment and more information, also see\n        </i>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_Kit_2-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Press_Kit-2">\n          [2]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S4_truss.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/S4_truss.jpg/220px-S4_truss.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/S4_truss.jpg/330px-S4_truss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/S4_truss.jpg/440px-S4_truss.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S4_truss.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         An overhead crane lifts the S3/S4 truss inside the Space Station Processing Facility\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The STS-117 mission delivered the second starboard truss segment (S3/S4) and associated energy systems to the International Space Station (ISS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_Kit_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Press_Kit-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Manufactured by The Boeing Company, S3/S4 is the heaviest station payload the shuttle has ever carried.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR5_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR5-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The main functions of the S3/S4 truss segments are to provide electrical power and data interfaces for station\'s electronics and convert sunlight to electricity. They also provide active thermal protection to electrical components throughout the space station and allow the connection of platforms to store spare parts. S3/S4 segments were the second starboard addition to the ISS truss structure after the S1 truss was attached during Atlantis\'\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-112" title="STS-112">\n        STS-112\n       </a>\n       mission.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Both S3/S4 were handed off to NASA in September 2002. S3/S3 measures 44 feet 9.6\xc2\xa0inches long by 16 feet 3.4\xc2\xa0inches wide by 15 feet 2.3\xc2\xa0inches high and weighs 35,678\xc2\xa0lbs.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During flight day 4 activities, the S3/S4 truss segment was removed from the payload bay of Atlantis using the shuttle\xe2\x80\x99s robotic arm and handed off to the station\'s Canadarm2, where it was maneuvered and mated to the outboard end of the S1 truss.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Starboard_3">\n        Starboard 3\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Starboard 3">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:070215_sts117_after_02.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/070215_sts117_after_02.jpg/220px-070215_sts117_after_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/070215_sts117_after_02.jpg/330px-070215_sts117_after_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/070215_sts117_after_02.jpg/440px-070215_sts117_after_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:070215_sts117_after_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Post STS-117 station configuration with the newly installed S3/S4 truss segment.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The S3 primary structure is made of a hexagonal-shaped aluminum structure and includes four bulkheads and six longerons, beams that connect the bulkheads. The secondary structure includes brackets, fittings, attach platforms, EVA activity equipment and miscellaneous mechanisms. S3 was delivered to the Space Station Processing Facility at Kennedy Space Center on 7 December 2000.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The major S3 subsystems include the Solar Array Rotary Joint (SARJ), Segment-to-Segment Attach System (SSAS) and Payload Attach System (PAS). The SARJ continuously rotates to keep the Solar Array Wings (SAWs) on S4 and S6 (launched on shuttle mission STS\xe2\x80\x90119 in March 2009) oriented toward the sun as the ISS orbits the Earth. The S3 also provides a passive attachment point to the S1 segment via the SSAS. The PAS allows platforms to be attached to S3 for the storage of additional science payloads or spare Orbital Replacement units (ORUs).\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Starboard_4">\n        Starboard 4\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Starboard 4">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Major subsystems of the S4 truss are the port inboard Photovoltaic Module (PVM), the Photovoltaic Radiator (PVR), the Alpha Joint Interface Structure (AJIS) and the Modified Rocketdyne Truss Attachment System (MRTAS). The primary functions of the PVMs are to collect, convert, store and distribute electrical power to loads within the segment and to other station segments. There are two SAWs on the S4 each deployed in the opposite direction from each other. Each SAW is made up of two solar blankets mounted to a common mast and measures 115 feet (35\xc2\xa0m) by 38 feet (12\xc2\xa0m). In addition to the SARJ, the SAWs also are oriented by the Beta Gimbal Assembly (BGA), which can change the pitch of the wings by spinning the solar array. The PVR is deployable on orbit and is capable of dissipating up to 14\xc2\xa0kW of heat into space. The PVR weighs 1,633 pounds and when deployed measures 44 by 12 by 7 feet (2.1\xc2\xa0m). The AJIS provides the structural transition between S3 and S4 structures. S4 contains the passive side of the MRTAS which provides the structural attachment for S5 on S4.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       S4 was delivered to the Space Station Processing Facility at Kennedy Space Center on 15 January 2001.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrogen_Vent_Valve">\n        Hydrogen Vent Valve\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hydrogen Vent Valve">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis carried a Hydrogen Vent Valve in its mid-deck to the space station. The valve used to vent Hydrogen overboard is part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxygen_generating_system" title="Oxygen generating system">\n        Oxygen Generation System\n       </a>\n       (OGS). The OGS helps to produce oxygen for the crew to replace oxygen lost due to experiment use, airlock depressurization and venting.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_items">\n        Other items\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other items">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Other items carried on the mid-deck included a contingency water container for transferring water to the ISS, a tool "modified torque multiplier" for removing S3 launch restraints and audio interface hardware to troubleshoot shuttle-to-station communication difficulties experienced during\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n        STS-115\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n        STS-116\n       </a>\n       . The payload weight for the mid-deck during STS-117 was less than 1,000 pounds.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Among numerous cargo,\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       carried into space an almost 400-year-old artifact (a metal cargo tag) etched with the name of its destination "Yames Towne" from historic Jamestown along with four commemorative coins to honor early American explorers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 17th-century metal worker had prepared a tag to mark cargo heading for the New World. The tag was unearthed in 2006 at Jamestown, the location of the first permanent English settlement in the Americas in 1607.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        A comprehensive list of STS-132 items that will be carried aboard Atlantis and their descriptions can be found in the Official Flight Kit\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_background">\n        Mission background\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mission background">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The mission marks:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ql_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ql-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        149th manned US space flight\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        118th shuttle mission since\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n         STS-1\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        28th flight of\n        <i>\n         Atlantis\n        </i>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        21st shuttle mission to the ISS\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1st shuttle flight in 2007\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        93rd post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n          Challenger\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        5th post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n          Columbia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shuttle_processing">\n        Shuttle processing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Shuttle processing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_Stack_Mating_(STS-117).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2000" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg/220px-Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg/330px-Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg/440px-Atlantis_Stack_Mating_%28STS-117%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantis_Stack_Mating_(STS-117).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         is mated to the rest of the STS-117 stack.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_rollback2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/STS-117_rollback2.jpg/220px-STS-117_rollback2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/STS-117_rollback2.jpg/330px-STS-117_rollback2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/STS-117_rollback2.jpg/440px-STS-117_rollback2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_rollback2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         being rolled back to the VAB for repairs on 4 March 2007, following hailstorm damage.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       STS-117 was originally planned to launch on 16 March, but the launch date was later moved forward in order to extend the launch window and increase the chances of a successful launch within that time frame. In preparation for this earlier launch date,\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       was transported to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       on 7 February 2007. First motion was at 06:19 EST.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the arrival of the shuttle in the assembly facility, Atlantis was fitted with two bridge cranes that lifted her vertically, to position her for mating to the external fuel tank and solid rocket boosters, already in place atop the mobile launcher platform. The mating of the Orbiter to the stack occurred on 12 February 2007. The rest of the pre-launch preparations also continued to proceed according to plans, with the payload canister, containing the S3/S4 Truss and a set of solar arrays, arriving at the launch pad at 02:54\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">\n        EST\n       </a>\n       on 12 February 2007. The canister lift began at 05:40 EST the same morning, ready for transfer of the ISS truss segments and other cargo into the Payload Changeout Room on the newly refurbished rotating service structure of pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       was originally scheduled to begin her rollout to launch pad 39A (the first shuttle launch at 39A in four years) on 14 February 2007, however due to erratic chamber pressure readings on one of the Operational Pressure Transducers (OPTs) on the forward skirt area of the right-hand SRB, the rollout was delayed to 07:00 EST on the morning of 15 February 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Various problems, including a generator transfer issue to the mobile launcher platform, meant that first movement of the stack was delayed from the scheduled rollout time and did not occur until 08:19 EST. The 3.4-mile (5.5\xc2\xa0km), six-hour journey to the launchpad concluded that afternoon, with\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       arriving at the launch pad at 15:09 EST. It was decided that the issue with the OPT would be solved on the launch pad, a task which may require all six transducers on the STS-117 stack being removed and replaced.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 21 February 2007, the STS-117 crew traveled from Houston to the Kennedy Space Center (KSC) to participate in the Terminal Countdown Demonstration Test (TCDT). The astronauts were at KSC from 21\xe2\x80\x9323 February 2007, during which time they practiced launch activities, carried out safety exercises, inspected the payload and concluded the test with a simulated main engine cut-off exercise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They then returned to Houston via T-38 jets, planning to return to KSC a few days before launch. The next milestone in the launch preparations was the Flight Readiness Review from 27\xe2\x80\x9328 February 2007, during which time managers, engineers and contractors examined the readiness of the Space Shuttle, flight crew and payloads to determine whether everything was set to proceed for launch.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hail_damage">\n        Hail damage\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hail damage">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg/220px-STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg/330px-STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg/440px-STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_ET_damage1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n          External tank (ET)-124\n         </a>\n         shows hailstorm damage.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_ETrepair.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/STS-117_ETrepair.jpg/220px-STS-117_ETrepair.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/STS-117_ETrepair.jpg/330px-STS-117_ETrepair.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/STS-117_ETrepair.jpg/440px-STS-117_ETrepair.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_ETrepair.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Technicians repair the ET nose cone.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Following a hailstorm at KSC on 26 February 2007, inspections of the stack found damage to the shuttle and the external tank. Hailstones as large as golf balls had created around 1,000\xe2\x80\x932,000 divots in the tank\'s foam insulation, damaged at least one Ice Frost Ramp on the tank, and caused minor surface damage to about 26 heat shield tiles on\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\'\n       </i>\n       s left wing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 4 March 2007 the STS-117 stack was similarly rolled back into the VAB. Following additional inspections, repairs to the orbiter and tank were carried out to return\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       to flight readiness. After completion of the repairs,\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       (along with her distinctly speckled external tank) was rolled out to pad 39A for the second time during the morning of 15 May 2007. A second Flight Readiness Review took place on 30\xe2\x80\x9331 May 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The hail damage to\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       caused major changes to the shuttle launch manifest at that time, pushing\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       back to 8 August 2007 (which could not have flown until the installation of the S3/S4 truss segment carried by\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       was completed),\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n        STS-120\n       </a>\n       back to 23 October 2007, and\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\'s\n       </i>\n       return on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">\n        STS-122\n       </a>\n       back to a targeted launch date on 6 December 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Atlantis on STS-122 eventually lifted off on 7 February 2008.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aging_problem">\n        Aging problem\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Aging problem">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis#Composite_overwrapped_pressure_vessels" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n        Space Shuttle Atlantis \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Composite overwrapped pressure vessels\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       NASA announced that it is possible, albeit unlikely, that one of 24 Composite Overwrap Pressure Vessels onboard Atlantis could burst before launch, damaging the orbiter. A burst of a vessel during launch could have resulted in the loss of the shuttle and crew. NASA changed the launch procedure for Atlantis to counter this problem and reduce any risk to personnel and the shuttle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_timeline">\n        Mission timeline\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mission timeline">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="8_June_(Flight_day_1_\xe2\x80\x93_Launch)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="8_June_.28Flight_day_1_.E2.80.93_Launch.29">\n        8 June (Flight day 1 \xe2\x80\x93 Launch)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 8 June (Flight day 1 \xe2\x80\x93 Launch)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1986" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg/200px-Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg/300px-Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg/400px-Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sts117_Atlantis_Launch1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         launches at the beginning of STS-117.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:320px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" style="width:320px;height:240px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="67.2" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" data-height="160" data-bandwidth="199040" data-framerate="25"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'>\n         <img alt="File:STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv/220px--STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:165px"/>\n         <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv" target="new" title="Play media">\n          <span class="play-btn-large">\n           <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">\n            Play media\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117-Launch-Jun8-2007.ogv" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <b>\n          Launch video\n         </b>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis was launched on schedule at 23:38:04 UTC from launch pad 39A at the KSC with NASA launch commentator\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Diller" title="George Diller">\n        George Diller\n       </a>\n       \'s words upon launch being "and Liftoff of Space Shuttle Atlantis, to assemble the framework for the science laboratories of tomorrow!".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       STS-117 was the first launch from launch pad 39A since the fateful\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       launch of space shuttle\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in 2003.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All pre-launch processing proceeded normally, and the crew started to board\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       at 16:17 EDT (20:17 UTC). Crew boarding was completed at 20:58 UTC, and the hatch was closed at around 21:40 UTC. Weather was 80%\n       <i>\n        go\n       </i>\n       to support the launch. There were concerns about the weather at\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_abort_modes" title="Space Shuttle abort modes">\n        TAL\n       </a>\n       abort landing sites, but\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Istres_Air_Base" title="Istres Air Base">\n        Istres\n       </a>\n       in France changed to\n       <i>\n        go\n       </i>\n       in time for the launch. The conditions at the other available site,\n       <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza_Airport" title="Zaragoza Airport">\n        Zaragoza\n       </a>\n       , were observed to be improving. The third TAL site,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mor%C3%B3n_Air_Base" title="Mor\xc3\xb3n Air Base">\n        Mor\xc3\xb3n AFB\n       </a>\n       , was closed for runway maintenance until 15 June 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Powered flight confirmed to the standard timeline (see\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle_launch" title="Space shuttle launch">\n        Space Shuttle \xe2\x80\x93 Mission Profile \xe2\x80\x93 Launch\n       </a>\n       ). Atlantis\' eight-and-a-half-minute ride to orbit was mostly uneventful with only one small piece of debris spotted just after solid rocket booster separation two minutes and five seconds after the launch. Shuttle Program Manager,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Hale" title="Wayne Hale">\n        Wayne Hale\n       </a>\n       said a preliminary analysis of launch video "indicates the debris didn\'t strike the orbiter".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       launched, the space station flew 220 miles (350\xc2\xa0km) above the southern Indian Ocean, southwest of Australia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Aboard the ISS, cosmonauts\n       <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Yurchikhin" title="Fyodor Yurchikhin">\n        Fyodor Yurchikhin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Kotov" title="Oleg Kotov">\n        Oleg Kotov\n       </a>\n       and NASA astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunita_Williams" title="Sunita Williams">\n        Sunita Williams\n       </a>\n       watched the launch of Atlantis on a video feed provided by flight controllers in Houston.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After reaching orbit, Atlantis\' crew began procedures to open the shuttle\xe2\x80\x99s payload bay doors and set up computers and other equipment. They also powered up the shuttle\'s robotic arm to check its operation. Photos taken during the robotic arm checkout showed a 4-inch by 6-inch corner area of insulation blanket on the shuttle\'s port orbital maneuvering system (OMS) pod pulled away from an adjacent row of heat-shield tiles.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Crew_head_to_AstroVan.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/STS117_Crew_head_to_AstroVan.jpg/120px-STS117_Crew_head_to_AstroVan.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/STS117_Crew_head_to_AstroVan.jpg/240px-STS117_Crew_head_to_AstroVan.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           STS-117 crewmembers head for the astrovan\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox"      </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_ET.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="79" </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Launch of Space Shuttle Atlantis viewed from the top of the Vehicle Assembly Building\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="9_June_(Flight_day_2_\xe2\x80\x93_TPS_survey)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="9_June_.28Flight_day_2_.E2.80.93_TPS_survey.29">\n        9 June (Flight day 2 \xe2\x80\x93 TPS survey)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 9 June (Flight day 2 \xe2\x80\x93 TPS survey)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="383" data-file-width="559" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg/220px-STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg/330px-STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg/440px-STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_OMS_blanket.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The peeled-back thermal blanket on OMS pod.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During its first full day in orbit, crewmembers aboard\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       inspected the shuttle\'s heat shield. The crew was given an extra half-hour to sleep after being kept up late to finish downloading in-cabin video.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Pilot Lee Archambault and Mission Specialists Patrick Forrester and Steven Swanson used the shuttle\'s robotic arm and orbiter boom sensor system (OBSS) to inspect the heat shield on Atlantis\xe2\x80\x99 wing leading edges and nose cap.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Based on lessons learned during the previous three post-Columbia missions, during STS-117, the crew used new inspection procedures devised by NASA. The scans took less time, covered a larger area and they used a camera on the end of the OBSS to take close-up photographs at the same time the laser scanner was collecting data.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The astronauts started with the starboard wing leading edge, making multiple passes up and down the wing to cover all the angles. After scanning the nose cap, they moved on to the port wing and repeated the procedure.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crew also down-linked Mission Control Houston engineers up-close video of the displaced portion of the blanket on the port orbital maneuvering system pod.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While the robotic arm survey proceeded, Mission Specialists \xe2\x80\x9cDanny\xe2\x80\x9d Olivas, James Reilly and Clayton Anderson conducted a thorough checkout of the spacesuits to be worn during the spacewalks planned for the docked operations at the space station and prepared them and other EVA hardware for transfer to the space station. The crew also installed a centerline camera, extend the outer ring of the Orbiter Docking System, and checked out rendezvous tools.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="10_June_(Flight_day_3_\xe2\x80\x93_Docking)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="10_June_.28Flight_day_3_.E2.80.93_Docking.29">\n        10 June (Flight day 3 \xe2\x80\x93 Docking)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 10 June (Flight day 3 \xe2\x80\x93 Docking)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1997" data-file-width="3027" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg/220px-STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg/330px-STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg/440px-STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS_117_overturned_shuttle.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space Shuttle\n         <i>\n          Atlantis\n         </i>\n         performs the RPM.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis\' crew was awakened at 13:08 UTC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Guided by the Terminal Insertion burn to refine the shuttle\'s trajectory\xe2\x80\x94Atlantis closed in on the ISS. Before the shuttle docked, at a distance of 600 feet (180\xc2\xa0m) below the station, STS-117 Commander Rick Sturckow performed what is known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rendezvous_Pitch_Maneuver" title="Rendezvous Pitch Maneuver">\n        Rendezvous Pitch Maneuver\n       </a>\n       (RPM). The back flip RPM allowed station crewmembers Fyodor Yurchikhin and Oleg Kotov to photograph heat shield tiles on the shuttle\'s underside using long-range, high resolution cameras.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       docked to Destiny/Pressurized Mating Adapter-2 on the ISS at 19:36 UTC while the two spacecraft were traveling 220 miles (350\xc2\xa0km) above the northeast coast of Australia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A few minutes later, hooks and latches were activated to firmly pull the two spacecraft together. After leak checks to make sure the interface is airtight, the hatch between them was opened at 21:20 UTC and the station crew welcomed the shuttle crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR5_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR5-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Shortly after welcoming the shuttle crew, station Flight Engineer Oleg Kotov and shuttle Mission Specialist Clayton Anderson transferred Anderson\'s customized Soyuz seat liner into the Russian spacecraft in place of that of Flight Engineer Suni Williams. The transfer marked the official swap of Anderson for Williams as a station crewmember.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following docking, Pilot Lee Archambault and Mission Specialist Patrick Forrester used the shuttle\'s Canadarm to grapple the S3/S4 truss, lift it from its berth in the payload bay, and maneuver it for handover to the station\'s Canadarm2. After hatch opening, Suni Williams used the Canadarm2 to take the truss from the shuttle\xe2\x80\x99s robotic arm. That task was completed at 00:28 UTC marking the completion of the handover. The truss remained grappled to the station\xe2\x80\x99s arm until next day\'s installation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mission Specialists James Reilly and John "Danny" Olivas spent the night in the Quest airlock as part of the overnight "campout" procedure to help them get prepared for next day\'s spacewalk.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_ISS_view.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/STS-117_ISS_view.jpg/120px-STS-117_ISS_view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/STS-117_ISS_view.jpg/180px-STS-117_ISS_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/STS-117_ISS_view.jpg/240px-STS-117_ISS_view.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           The ISS seen from\n           <i>\n            Atlantis\n           </i>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg/120px-STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg/180px-STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg/240px-STS117_crew_give_packages.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           The STS-117 crewmembers give the station crewmembers packages\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="11_June_(Flight_day_4_\xe2\x80\x93_EVA_1)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="11_June_.28Flight_day_4_.E2.80.93_EVA_1.29">\n        11 June (Flight day 4 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 1)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 11 June (Flight day 4 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 1)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1954" data-file-width="3000" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg/220px-S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg/330px-S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg/440px-S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S3-S4_Truss_Installed_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mission Specialists Reilly and Olivas participates in EVA 1.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Pilot Archambault, Mission Specialist Forrester and station Flight Engineer\n       <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Kotov" title="Oleg Kotov">\n        Kotov\n       </a>\n       used the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSRMS" title="SSRMS">\n        SSRMS\n       </a>\n       to mate the S3/S4 truss to the outboard end of the S1 truss. The installation paved the way for the start of the spacewalk planned for the day.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After venturing out of the Quest airlock into space, Mission Specialists Reilly and Olivas released launch restraints on the four Solar Array Blanket Boxes, which house the folded solar arrays. They made final attachment of bolts, cables and connectors, and began preparations for the activation of the truss. The two spacewalkers rotated the array canisters into their normal position for deployment on the next day. The start of the spacewalk was delayed for about an hour after the station temporarily lost attitude control when the station\xe2\x80\x99s\n       <a href="/wiki/Control_moment_gyroscope" title="Control moment gyroscope">\n        control moment gyroscopes\n       </a>\n       (CMGs) went offline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The spacewalk started after station\'s gyroscopes were initialized by flight controllers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       EVA 1 marked the 84th devoted to the ISS assembly and maintenance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was also the fourth for Reilly and first for Olivas.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA\'s Mission Management Team also decided to extend Atlantis\' mission by two days and to add a fourth spacewalk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       John Shannon, the head of NASA\'s STS-117 Mission Management Team during the day\'s mission briefing told reporters that the extra time would give the crew to complete the ISS assembly tasks and allow ground engineers to draw up plans to repair the damaged blanket on the OMS pod of Atlantis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA deemed that the torn blanket, while not a flight risk to the shuttle crew during reentry, could lead to some damage to the OMS pod\'s internal honeycomb-like graphite-epoxy structure. Such a damage would require additional time to repair once the Shuttle returns to Earth, NASA said.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_EVA1d.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/STS-117_EVA1d.jpg/120px-STS-117_EVA1d.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/STS-117_EVA1d.jpg/180px-STS-117_EVA1d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/STS-117_EVA1d.jpg/240px-STS-117_EVA1d.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           James Reilly (left) and John Olivas during EVA 1\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_EVA1b.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-117_EVA1b.jpg/120px-STS-117_EVA1b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-117_EVA1b.jpg/180px-STS-117_EVA1b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/STS-117_EVA1b.jpg/240px-STS-117_EVA1b.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Astronaut James Reilly participate in EVA 1\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2014" data-file-width="3032" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg/120px-STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg/180px-STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg/240px-STS117_Reilly_Olivas_EVA1.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           James Reilly (right) and John Olivas during EVA 1\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="12_June_(Flight_day_5_\xe2\x80\x93_Solar_array_deployment)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="12_June_.28Flight_day_5_.E2.80.93_Solar_array_deployment.29">\n        12 June (Flight day 5 \xe2\x80\x93 Solar array deployment)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 12 June (Flight day 5 \xe2\x80\x93 Solar array deployment)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg/220px-STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg/330px-STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg/440px-STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Crew_Flight_Day5.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         STS-117 crewmembers in the Destiny laboratory.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The successful deployment of the S3/S4 solar arrays was the highlight of the day, adding significantly to the ISS power generation capabilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prior to crew wake up, station controllers began unfurling the solar array attached to the S3/S4 truss segment. Shuttle crew then took over, unfolding one wing at a time in stages, pausing to let the sun warm the solar array panels which helped to prevent the thin individual panels from sticking together.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The crew finished unfolding the first wing at 11:29\xc2\xa0am CDT and the second at 12:58\xc2\xa0pm CDT.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were continuing problems with the station\'s electrically-driven gyroscopes, the preferred, non-propulsive, method for controlling the ISS due to a problem with a Russian navigation computer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The navigation computer problem started when flight controllers attempted to turn attitude control over to the ISS computers after letting shuttle computers handle it while the arrays were unfolded. The navigation computer would not allow them to do so, and forced a reboot of the main Russian command and control computer. The forced reboot triggered an alarm enunciating the problem to the crew and ground controllers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The issues appeared to have been resolved by the end of the day and the station\'s gyroscopes took over attitude control shortly after 8\xc2\xa0pm CDT. That was followed by relocation of the Mobile Transporter in preparation ahead the next day\'s spacewalk. The crew or shuttle/station combined stack never was in danger throughout the troubleshooting efforts.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="13_June_(Flight_day_6_\xe2\x80\x93_EVA_2)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="13_June_.28Flight_day_6_.E2.80.93_EVA_2.29">\n        13 June (Flight day 6 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 2)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 13 June (Flight day 6 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 2)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg/220px-STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg/330px-STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg/440px-STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_Swanson_EVA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Astronaut Steven Swanson participates in EVA 2\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Flight day 6 saw mission specialists Patrick Forrester and Steven Swanson perform the second of four planned spacewalks. The main task of the spacewalk was to prepare the Solar Alpha Rotary Joint (SARJ) between the S3 and S4 Truss segments for rotation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The two spacewalkers and their crew mates were awakened at 13:08 UTC to begin the day\'s activities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mission Specialists John Olivas and Sunita Williams helped Forrester and Swanson to get readied with the EVA. Commander Sturckow, pilot Archambault and Mission Specialist Jim Reilly worked the early steps of retraction of the 2B solar array wing, on the starboard side of the P6 Truss. They sent commands and monitored the retraction.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After exiting Quest at 18:03 UTC the two spacewalkers moved up the P6 Truss to monitor the retraction of the 2B Sollar Array and to assist if required. Forrester, was in a foot restraint on the station\'s Canadarm2, and Swanson had specially-prepared tools to use to help the panels of photovoltaic cells fold properly. Flight controllers were able to get seven and a half of the 31.5 solar array bays folded. Then, Forrester and Swanson were able to poke and prod another five and a half bays worth of panels into folding correctly (some 45 feet) before moving on to the SARJ.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Forrester and Swanson completed EVA 2 with mixed results.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The duo removed all of the launch locks holding the SARJ in place. The spacewalkers had planned to remove the SARJ\xe2\x80\x99s launch restraints as well, but ran into problem when Forrester tried to install a drive-lock assembly. They discovered that the S3/S4 SARJ motor control circuits were wired in reverse. As such commands being sent to the drive-lock assembly were actually being received by a drive-lock assembly that was installed during EVA 1. So one launch lock restraint was left in place to prevent the possibility of undesired rotation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       EVA 2 marked the 85th spacewalk devoted to station assembly and maintenance.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As EVA 2 progressed, Mission managers approved a repair task for the damaged thermal blanket to be carried out during the next spacewalk, EVA 3. Overnight the Russian flight controllers also worked to resolve the problem with the Russian segment computers. During the day, with the shuttle\xe2\x80\x99s propulsion providing backup, the station\xe2\x80\x99s control moment gyroscopes were handling attitude control.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg/120px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg/180px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg/240px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA2_preparations.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Mission Specialists Swanson and Forrester in the midst of the pre-breathe exercise\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_EVA2c.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="79" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/STS-117_EVA2c.jpg/240px-STS-117_EVA2c.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Mission Specialist Patrick Forrester during EVA 2\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg/120px-STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg/180px-STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg/240px-STS117_EVA2_Steven_Swanson.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Mission Specialist Steven Swanson during EVA 2\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image"
