//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/STS117_crew_completion_of_EVA2.jpg/240px-STS117_crew_completion_of_EVA2.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Crew members give a "thumbs-up" signal at the conclusion of EVA 2\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="14_June_(Flight_day_7)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="14_June_.28Flight_day_7.29">\n        14 June (Flight day 7)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 14 June (Flight day 7)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station#2007_Computer_Failure" title="International Space Station">\n        computer malfunction on the Russian segments\n       </a>\n       of the ISS occurred at 06:30 UTC and left the space station without orientation control. A successful restart of the computers resulted in a false fire alarm which awakened the crew at 11:43 UTC. Engineers theorized that the new S4 solar array, or components in the circuitry delivering that power to the Russian segment of the ISS, triggered some subtle change in the ISS electrical grid.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The solar array blanket atop the P6 truss was furled to a little more than half its original length by the\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       and the station crews. Commander Rick Sturckow, along with Pilot Lee Archambault, Mission Specialist Sunita Williams and Flight Engineer Clayton Anderson, meticulously retracted the solar array blanket another three bays worth of panels. The crew carefully sent commands to retract the array as much as possible ahead of EVA 3. By last count, 15 and a half of the 31 and half bays remained to be folded into a 20-inch-deep protective box.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mission Specialists James Reilly and John Olivas completed a review of procedures for EVA 3. Before going to sleep, the crew also talked about the mission with radio and television stations. After that Reilly and Olivas slept in the Quest Airlock for spacewalk pre-breathe campout protocol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="15_June_(Flight_day_8_\xe2\x80\x93_EVA_3)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="15_June_.28Flight_day_8_.E2.80.93_EVA_3.29">\n        15 June (Flight day 8 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 3)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 15 June (Flight day 8 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 3)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2020" data-file-width="3032" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg/220px-STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg/330px-STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg/440px-STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Danny_Olivas_EVA3.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Astronaut John Olivas moves toward Atlantis\' port OMS pod.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The crew\xe2\x80\x99s wakeup call came at 7:41\xc2\xa0am CDT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Flight day 8 was dedicated to mission\'s third spacewalk (EVA 3) to repair the thermal blanket on\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       and assist in folding up a solar array on the space station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Spacewalkers James Reilly and John Olivas began EVA 3 when the two astronauts switched their spacesuits into internal battery power and exited into space from the Quest airlock. It was the 86th EVA dedicated to ISS assembly and maintenance and the ninth for year 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While Olivas anchored to the end of Atlantis\' robot arm was repairing the OMS pod, Reilly installed an external hydrogen vent for the oxygen generating system inside\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destiny_Laboratory_Module" title="Destiny Laboratory Module">\n         Destiny\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       laboratory. By using his\n       <a href="/wiki/Helmet_camera" title="Helmet camera">\n        helmet camera\n       </a>\n       , Olivas beamed down close-up views of the torn insulation and surrounding blankets to help flight controllers assess the system\'s condition. Olivas spent two hours stapling and pinning down a thermal blanket on the OMS pod.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Flight controllers from Houston also radioed Reilly that they had decided to have him disconnect the P-12 connector that was installed during EVA 1 since the Russian flight controllers were planning to make an attempt to restart the problematic computers in the ISS. Even though the connector was not in use at that time, engineers decided to have Reilly disconnect it to make sure that it was not causing any electrical noise or grounding issues that might have played a role in the computer trouble.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When those tasks were completed, the two astronauts along with their colleagues inside the shuttle and station and flight controllers in Houston completed the final retraction of the starboard P6 truss element. The retraction that required 28 commands was completed and latches closed seven hours, 15 minutes into the spacewalk at 7:40\xc2\xa0pm CDT. The successful folding paved the way to relocate the P6 truss to its permanent location during\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n        STS-120\n       </a>\n       . All tasks were completed successfully on during the 7 hours, 58-minute EVA activities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Earlier on the day, U.S. and Russian engineers disconnected U.S. electrical power from the Russian computer system. But isolating the computers from U.S. power did not resolve the problem. The primary Russian computers were brought back online by bypassing a circuit. Secondary systems were left offline pending further work.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR15_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR15-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114-3b_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114-3b-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35.5px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_EVA3c.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/STS-117_EVA3c.jpg/120px-STS-117_EVA3c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/STS-117_EVA3c.jpg/180px-STS-117_EVA3c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/STS-117_EVA3c.jpg/240px-STS-117_EVA3c.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Astronauts James Reilly (on robot arm) and John Olivas during EVA 3\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2011" data-file-width="3032" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg/120px-STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg/180px-STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg/240px-STS117_FD8_Patrick_Forrester.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Patrick Forrester talks to ground controllers while on the aft flight deck of Atlantis\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:36px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="1979" data-file-width="3032" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg/120px-STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg/180px-STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg/240px-STS117_Reilly_Enters_Quest_Airlock.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           James Reilly enters the Quest Airlock at the conclusion of EVA 3\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="16_June_(Flight_day_9)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="16_June_.28Flight_day_9.29">\n        16 June (Flight day 9)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 16 June (Flight day 9)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2064" data-file-width="3032" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg/220px-STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg/330px-STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg/440px-STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_Crew_Press_Photo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The shuttle and space station crew poses for a press photo.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="rquote floatleft" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:left; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">\n       <tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">\n        <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:\'Times New Roman\',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9c\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding:0 10px;">\n         I was just in the right place at the right time. It\'s an honor to be here.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR17_50-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR17-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         \xe2\x80\x94- Astronaut Sunita Williams sets up a new space endurance record\n        </td>\n        <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:\'Times New Roman\',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">\n         \xe2\x80\x9d\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The crew of\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       had a day of light duties. Earlier on the day Astronaut Sunita Williams set a new space endurance record for female astronauts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At 5:47 UTC on flight day 9, Mission Specialist Williams\' time in space reached 188 days and 4 hours, matching the mark for the longest single spaceflight ever by a woman space traveler.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR16_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR16-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       That mark was set by Astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Lucid" title="Shannon Lucid">\n        Shannon Lucid\n       </a>\n       on her flight to the Mir space station in 1996. By coincidence, Williams also set the new record on the 44th anniversary of the launch of the first female space flyer\n       <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Tereshkova" title="Valentina Tereshkova">\n        Valentina Tereshkova\n       </a>\n       in 1963.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Crew members spent time transferring supplies between ISS and\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       . Later on the day they reviewed the timeline for next day\'s spacewalk. Mission Specialists James Reilly, John Olivas, Steven Swanson and Patrick Forrester spent time working on the U.S. spacesuits. Olivas and Reilly finished their post-spacewalk spacesuit reconfiguration tasks, while Forrester and Swanson configured their suits and tools for EVA 4.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle and space station crew also spoke with reporters during a space-to-ground news conference.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Earlier in the day, flight controllers in Moscow issued commands to restart some systems in the Russian segment of the space station. During the day computer problems on the ISS were further resolved, with all six processors available (four online and two standby).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR17_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR17-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Following the successful attempt to revive four channels on flight day 8 after bypassing what appeared to be a faulty power switch with external cabling, cosmonauts Fyodor Yurchikhin and Oleg Kotov repeated that same modification on the last two channels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="17_June_(Flight_day_10_\xe2\x80\x93_EVA_4)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="17_June_.28Flight_day_10_.E2.80.93_EVA_4.29">\n        17 June (Flight day 10 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 4)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 17 June (Flight day 10 \xe2\x80\x93 EVA 4)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2012" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg/220px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg/330px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg/440px-STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS117_Swanson_Forrester_EVA4.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mission specialists Patrick Forrester (left) and Steven Swanson participate in EVA 4.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The crew\'s wakeup call went up at 6:38\xc2\xa0am CDT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR18_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR18-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Flight day 10 saw the successful completion of the mission\'s final spacewalk by Patrick Forrester and Steven Swanson.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The fourth\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n        spacewalk\n       </a>\n       of STS-117 began at 16:25 UTC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Astronaut James Reilly choreographed the activity from Atlantis\' flight deck shadowed by station Flight Engineer Oleg Kotov serving as the intravehicular crew member. EVA 4 was the 87th in support of station assembly and maintenance, 11th spacewalk completed in 2007, the 59th staged out of the ISS and the 36th out of the Quest airlock.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR19_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR19-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Swanson and Forrester retrieved a TV camera and its support structure from a stowage platform attached to the Quest Airlock and installed it on the S3 truss. They then verified the Drive Lock Assembly (DLA) 2 configuration and removed the last six SARJ launch restraints.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The two astronauts cleared the path on the S3 truss for the Mobile Base System by removing temporary rail stops and hardware that had secured the S3/S4 truss segments in the shuttle\xe2\x80\x99s payload bay. The work completed the major tasks assigned for the STS-117 mission.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The pair then began some of the get-ahead tasks mission managers had hoped to complete. The two spacewalkers installed a computer network cable on the Unity node that was to permit astronauts in the U.S. segment of the station to command systems in the Russian segment and opened the Hydrogen vent valve on the Destiny laboratory installed by Mission Specialist James Reilly during EVA 3. Swanson and Forrester also attempted to bolt down two debris shield panels that could not be put back in place during an earlier spacewalk. since the two were also not able to get it anchored, they tethered the panels on the space station\'s service module.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Overnight, ground controllers planned to test the SARJ, ordering a small 5-degree rotation just to verify normal operations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Throughout flight day 10, the Russian central computer and terminal computers continued in stable operation.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="18_June_(Flight_day_11_\xe2\x80\x93_Off-duty)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="18_June_.28Flight_day_11_.E2.80.93_Off-duty.29">\n        18 June (Flight day 11 \xe2\x80\x93 Off-duty)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 18 June (Flight day 11 \xe2\x80\x93 Off-duty)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       STS-117 crew got up looking ahead to time off duty during the first half of flight day 11. The astronauts hauled the last bits of cargo between the shuttle and the space station while flight controllers on Earth tested the station\xe2\x80\x99s resuscitated Russian control and navigation computers after they crashed last week. In the morning the shuttle maneuvered the Atlantis/ISS complex into position for a water and waste water dump and after it maneuvered back, attitude control was switched to and from Russian command successfully.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       was given a green light for undocking on flight day 12. Expedition 15 and Atlantis\'s crew said Farewells and sealed the hatches between the shuttle and the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="19_June_(Flight_day_12_\xe2\x80\x93_Undocking)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="19_June_.28Flight_day_12_.E2.80.93_Undocking.29">\n        19 June (Flight day 12 \xe2\x80\x93 Undocking)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 19 June (Flight day 12 \xe2\x80\x93 Undocking)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2007" data-file-width="3032" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg/220px-ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg/330px-ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg/440px-ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-117_in_June_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The International Space Station after completion of STS-117.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The astronauts on Atlantis woke up to begin flight day 12 with the hatch to the space station closed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 12:45 UTC Pilot Archambault and Mission Specialist Patrick Forrester began powering on shuttle systems that have been turned off to conserve power during the docked phase of the mission. At 13:28 UTC, Mission Specialists Steven Swanson and James Reilly installed the centerline camera in the Orbiter Docking System.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 9:42\xc2\xa0am the hooks and latches holding Atlantis and ISS together were released, and the shuttle undocked from the Space Station as the two spacecraft were flying above New Guinea.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Atlantis was docked to the station for 8 days and 19 hours. Pilot Lee Archambault took control of Atlantis shortly after undocking and fired shuttle thrusters to move 450 feet (140\xc2\xa0m) in front of the ISS before starting a full fly around at 15:07 UTC. Crew members on both the ISS and shuttle got photos of both spacecraft as Atlantis performed the fly around and once it was complete, the shuttle left of the vicinity of the station complex.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the separation, a camera in the cargo of Atlantis bay observed numerous objects what could have been harmless pieces of ice and one much larger, more distinct piece of debris slowly floating away. It was not clear whether the objects originated from the shuttle or the space station. Around 21:30 UTC, Commander Sturckow reported yet another piece of debris leaving the area of Atlantis. Sturckow identified them to the mission control in Houston as "little phenolic-looking, kind of tan-looking washers with four slots" that are used to tie down the Multi-Layer Insulation blankets in the payload bay.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Later in the day, Pilot Archambault, Mission Specialists Forrester and Swanson used the shuttle\'s robot arm to lift the Orbiter Boom Sensor System to conduct a late inspection of the thermal protection system on both wings and the orbiter\'s nose cap.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the day, Astronaut Sunita Williams, in the 192nd day of her spaceflight, did more exercise to help prepare her to gravity back on Earth.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="20_June_(Flight_day_13)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20_June_.28Flight_day_13.29">\n        20 June (Flight day 13)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 20 June (Flight day 13)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis did various hardware tests to prepare for a landing on 21 June 2007 and the crew had an interview with several large TV networks.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="21_June_(Flight_day_14_\xe2\x80\x93_Scrubbed_landing)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="21_June_.28Flight_day_14_.E2.80.93_Scrubbed_landing.29">\n        21 June (Flight day 14 \xe2\x80\x93 Scrubbed landing)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 21 June (Flight day 14 \xe2\x80\x93 Scrubbed landing)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis closed its payload bay doors and made various preparations for landing, but had to stay in orbit after both landing opportunities at Kennedy Space Center were scrubbed due to bad weather conditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR27_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR27-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="22_June_(Flight_day_15_\xe2\x80\x93_Landing)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="22_June_.28Flight_day_15_.E2.80.93_Landing.29">\n        22 June (Flight day 15 \xe2\x80\x93 Landing)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 22 June (Flight day 15 \xe2\x80\x93 Landing)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_landing.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-117_landing.jpg/200px-STS-117_landing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-117_landing.jpg/300px-STS-117_landing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-117_landing.jpg/400px-STS-117_landing.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-117_landing.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Atlantis lands on Runway 22 at Edwards AFB at the end of STS-117.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Flight day 15 saw Space Shuttle Atlantis returned to Earth after a successful mission to the Space Station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Earlier in the day, the flight controllers kept a close eye on weather. Atlantis again closed its payload bay doors and made preparations for landing. Atlantis had five opportunities to land (two at Kennedy Space Center, three at Edwards Air Force Base, California).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR29_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR29-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first and second landing attempts on Orbit 218 and 219 in Florida were scrubbed due to showers, thunderstorms and low clouds at Kennedy Space Center. So flight controllers took their first chance at Edwards Air Force Base, where weather was ideal for the landing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Flying upside down and backward over the Indian Ocean, the deorbit burn was initiated by Commander Rick Sturckow and Pilot Lee Archambault. They fired Atlantis\' twin OMS Pods at 18:43:47 UTC for 2 minutes and 33 seconds, slowing the ship by about 200\xc2\xa0mph.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was enough to drop the shuttle into the atmosphere for an hour-long glide back to Earth.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As the shuttle descended through 50,000 feet (15,000\xc2\xa0m), Commander Sturckow took over manual control and guided Atlantis successfully to land on Runway 22 at Edwards Air Force Base at 19:49:38 UTC. Flight surgeons were standing by to assist astronaut Sunita Williams, who made the trip back to Earth resting on her back in a recumbent seat bolted to the floor of the shuttle\'s lower deck. During her long duration flight Williams spent 194 days, 18 hours, 58 minutes in space.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Atlantis made 219 orbits and covered 5.8\xc2\xa0million miles during the flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MCCSR30_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MCCSR30-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A welcoming ceremony for the crew\'s return to Houston was held on 23 June at NASA Hangar 276 at Ellington Field.\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div           </a>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spacewalks">\n        Spacewalks\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n        Extra-vehicular activity\n They installed a rotary joint drive-lock assembly (DLA-1) and released latches allowing a folding radiator panel to extend as required.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="2">\n         EVA 2\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Patrick_G._Forrester" title="Patrick G. Forrester tried to install a drive-lock assembly (DLA 2) and found that commands being sent to it were actually being received by DLA 1. The spacewalkers also helped to partly retract the P6 solar array. They were able to poke and prod five and a half bays worth of panels into folding correctly.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="2">\n         EVA 3\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         James F. When those tasks were completed, Reilly and Olivas provided hands-on assistance to retract the P6 solar array into its protective box.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="2">\n         EVA 4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Patrick G. They then verified the Drive Lock Assembly (DLA) 2 configuration and removed the last six SARJ launch restraints. The two astronauts also installed a computer network cable on the Unity node, opened the hydrogen vent valve on the Destiny laboratory, and tethered two orbital debris shield panels on the station\'s service module.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wake-up_calls">\n        Wake-up calls\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Wake-up calls">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In what has become a tradition for NASA spaceflights since the days of\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Gemini\n       </a>\n       , the crew of STS-117 is played a special musical track at the start of each day in space. Each track is specially chosen and often has a particular meaning to an individual member of the crew, or it is somehow applicable to their situation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Flight Day\n     Day 12\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x9c\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feelin%E2%80%99_Stronger_Every_Day" title="Feelin\xe2\x80\x99 Stronger Every Day">\n          Feelin\xe2\x80\x99 Stronger Every Day\n         </a>\n         \xe2\x80\x9d\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Chicago\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Lee Archambault\n        </td>\n    </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_insignia">\n        Mission insignia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mission insignia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       STS-117 crew patch symbolizes the continued construction of the space station and ongoing human presence in space. The ISS is shown orbiting high above the Earth. Gold is used to highlight the portion of the ISS that will be installed by the STS-117 crew. The names of the STS-117 crew are located above and below the orbiting outpost. The two gold astronaut office symbols, emanating from the \'117\' at the bottom of the patch, represent the concerted efforts of the shuttle and station programs toward the completion of the station. The orbiter and unfurled banner of red, white, and blue represent the renewed patriotism of the American Nation as they continue to explore the universe.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contingency_planning">\n        Contingency planning\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Contingency planning">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-3xx" title="STS-3xx">\n        STS-3xx\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="STS-317">\n        STS-317\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: STS-317">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-3xx" title="STS-3xx">\n        STS-317\n       </a>\n       was the designation given to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contingency_Shuttle_Crew_Support" title="Contingency Shuttle Crew Support">\n        Contingency Shuttle Crew Support\n       </a>\n       mission which would have been launched in the event\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       became disabled during STS-116. It would have been a modified version of the STS-117 mission, which would have involved the launch date being brought forward. If needed, it would have launched no earlier than 21 February 2007. The crew for this mission would have been a 4-person subset of the full STS-117 crew.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Incorrect_press_reports_of_accident">\n        Incorrect press reports of accident\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Incorrect press reports of accident">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       On 9 June 2007, the French news agency\n       <a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">\n        Agence France-Presse\n       </a>\n       (AFP) reported that Atlantis had exploded shortly after take-off.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20min_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20min-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frogsmoke_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frogsmoke-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The information circulated on their wire for a number of minutes, and appeared on a number of websites including\n       <a href="/wiki/Lib%C3%A9ration" title="Lib\xc3\xa9ration">\n        Lib\xc3\xa9ration\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.romandie.com/news/" rel="nofollow">\n        Romandie News\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was later reported that AFP had prepared this sort of bulletin for every shuttle launch since the 1986\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Challenger disaster\n       </a>\n       and accidentally published it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frogsmoke_75-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frogsmoke-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is equivalent to accidental automated press releases in the past, such as the infamous case of\n       <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">\n        NBC\n       </a>\n       erroneously reporting\n       <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">\n        Joe DiMaggio\n       </a>\n       \'s death in 1999, about six weeks before his actual death.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-117&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n       <ul
